Software Tools
A basic configuration is included, and can be customized.

10

•

Easergy Builder: engineering tool for the RTU OFFLINE configuration. It
allows to include and adapt the different functions of the RTU to the system
where it is integrated.

•

CAE: engineering tool to define the security policy and assign roles to users. It
allows the definition of a series of rights and responsibilities in the system for
authorized users. It defines who, what, when and how to perform tasks
according to the Role-Based Access Configurations (RBAC) model. It is a
software tool that needs to be installed on a PC.

webApp First Contact

webApp - Maintenance and Monitoring Tool

•

webApp: web tool for online maintenance and monitoring of the RTU. Using
the configuration defined in Easergy Builder and loaded in the RTU, you can
refer and/or change some parameters through the web server. Unlike Easergy
Builder, webApp does not allow adding new features. Only the parameters
included in the configuration can be changed.

•

ESM: EcoStruxure™ System Management tool that provides an Inventory
Baseline Management (IBM) software, capable to perform maintenance on
connected equipment, in an heterogeneous solution with a focus on
cybersecurity:

•

BQT7944802-01

◦

Data Management: storage and backup while tracking the evolution of
Firmware, Configuration, Setting Files and Documentation.

◦

Manages firmware and configuration upload.

◦

Monitors real-time changes firmware and configuration version for
connected devices.

◦

Cybersecurity: manages Role-Based Access Configurations for Schneider
Electric devices.

◦

Collects Syslogs from Schneider Electric connected devices.

webUI: web-based graphical substation user interface. This tool can be used
in two different environments:
◦

webUI (run-time): web tool running in the RTU, used to monitor and control
the information using screens previously designed by the user with the
configuration tool.

◦

webUI Add-on: edition tool included in Easergy Builder for creating and
editing customized webUI screens. It is used to design new screens for the
configuration loaded into the RTU or also modify the information displayed
in those already available.

Monitoring & Control
Use the Monitoring & Control menu to monitor the system information and
control data in coreDb.

System Information Page
Select Monitoring & Control > System Information:
System information (showing missing information)

All information shown in this window is supplied by the supervision device. Each
supervision point must be included in the configuration if you need to monitor the
data in real time. If a point is not included in the configuration, a notice is shown.
In the above example, you can see the following notices:
•

Configuration zone: PLC information not available. The point FAIL_PLC is
not included in the loaded configuration or an ISaGRAF device is not included.

•

CPU usage: N/A: the point CPU USAGE is not included in coreDb.

•

RAM usage: N/A: the point RAM USAGE is not included in coreDb.

In Easergy Builder,
1. create an ISaGRAF device,
2. select points FAIL_PLC, CPU_USAGE, and MEM_USAGE for supervision
device,
3. send this configuration to the RTU for the information to be available in
webApp.

BQT7944802-01

Working with webApp

webApp - Maintenance and Monitoring Tool

Working with webApp
Access to webApp
Introduction
The RTU module is provided with a standard security policy and a default RBAC
(Role-Based Access Control) model.
This model is defined and managed by a special tool - CAE (EcoStruxure
Cybersecurity Admin Expert - Security Administration Tool). Based on this model,
using webApp, authorized users can create and manage other users in the
system.

CAE and RBAC model
The CAE is the security administration tool for managing the security policy and
defining the restrictions for accessing the system or the communication interfaces.
The CAE is a software tool to be installed on a PC.
The RTU security policy consists in structuring the rights and responsibilities
within the system and defining who is authorized to do what, when, and how,
based on an RBAC (role-based access control) model.
A key aspect of the RBAC model is that any access is controlled by roles. A role is
essentially a set of permissions that you receive by the role to which you are
assigned, or by the roles that you inherit through the hierarchy of roles.
This RBAC model allows the RTU to:
•

Secure local and remote connections for maintenance: HTTPS, SSH (only
available for SM_CPU866e and HUe).

•

Secure file transfer protocols: SFTP (only available for SM_CPU866e and
HUe).

The RTU is supplied with a predefined RBAC model allowing different levels of
user access adapted to the CPU usage compliant with standard IEC 62351-8.
It is not necessary to modify the default RBAC model if it is suitable. The CAE is
not used for general use of the modules. The CAE can be used to create its own
user database along with definition of its own roles, as well as to manage the
RBAC models for each device centrally.

Default Users
The CAE tool can be used during the engineering phase to define or change the
system access restrictions, including the access rights and responsibilities (based
on an RBAC model).
Since the roles and access levels are already predefined in the RBAC model,
webApp is used to add or delete users, modify passwords, and assign or modify
one or more predefined roles to users.
In the default user database, the SecurityAdmin user is the only user with
sufficient rights (SECADM role) to manage cybersecurity actions. Only this user
can manage/modify user passwords and rights (roles).
You cannot modify the rights assigned to a role using webApp.

•

•

A minimum length of 12 characters

Since the default password is not aligned with previous requirements, it cannot be
reused.

Roles
RBAC (Role-based-access-control) is a control mechanism that defines roles
which have certain privileges. These privileges are defined by objects and the
action that you can do with them.

System Security Parameters
The Cybersecurity involves a certain number of system parameters that are
applied to the security policy. These parameters are summarized in the table
below and can be modified in the CAE tool.
Parameter

Description

Idle session timeout

After a period of inactivity, your access to the web server lapses. You must re-enter their username
and password to reconnect (Default: 15 minutes).

Authorize user lockout

The option is to lock/unlock a user account (Default: Authorized).

Maximum number of connections

The maximum number of connections attempts you can make (Default: 5 attempts).

Password timeout

The maximum time period allowed for entering password (Default: 3 minutes).

Account auto-unlock

Automatic unlocking of a user account after a defined duration (see below) if the account has been
locked out (Default: unlocking enabled).

Account lock duration

The maximum time period for an account to remain locked (Default: 240 seconds).

WARNING
HAZARD OF EDITING LOCKED VALUES
Ensure that any locked and edited data values are valid to avoid an impact on
the control sequences of the system.
Failure to follow these instructions can result in death, serious injury or
equipment damage.

Click the
button associated with the Value field to manually edit the state or
value of a Command or Setpoint data item.
For a Status or Analog data item, you can force the status or value. This type of
data is only processed in read mode; forcing is only applied in simulation. To do
this, the actual data item must be locked first by clicking the Locking option.
Once the data is locked, the Edit button for this point is enabled and you can
change the status or value of the point in simulation mode.

42

BQT7944802-01

Working with webApp

webApp - Maintenance and Monitoring Tool

Disabling the Locking option cancels the simulation and returns to the actual
status or value of the data item.

Quality Information
Two icons displayed in the Quality column indicate the data processing quality.
The quality of a data item can indicate the validity of the status or value entered on
the web server page.
The quality is indicated for the following two sources:
•

Local source: reflects the quality of the data item from the viewpoint of its
processing at the CPU end.

•

Remote source: reflects the quality of the data item sent by the information
source (device) processing the data.

In the same way as for a change of state or value for Status or Analog data, you
can manually simulate the quality of a data item. To do this, first lock the data item
using the Locking option. Then click the
button associated with the Quality
field. The possible choices for the local and remote source quality are then
displayed on the screen.

Diagnostic and Maintenance
Introduction
NOTE: The features available in Diagnostic and Maintenance page depend
on the user’s role and rights.
The Diagnostic menu is used to view the data logs recorded in real time by the
RTU: events, system log, TCP traffic, or cybersecurity log (Security administration
rights are required).
The Maintenance menu helps with maintenance of the RTU: users management
(Security administration rights are required), system clock, IP configuration,
software upgrade and configuration management.

Diagnostic
Events Log Page

Events log

•

•

Filtered, by typing the text to search in the textbox under the name of the
column.

•

Cleared, by using

•

Exported to a csv file and downloaded to the PC.

button.

IMPORTANT: Be careful while clearing the events.
Take into account that clearing events do not only clear the table but also the
content of the SOE files in the file system. Events cannot be recovered after
confirming deletion.

IP Configuration
Select Maintenance > IP Configuration to access the IP Configuration page.

BQT7944802-01

53

webApp - Maintenance and Monitoring Tool

Working with webApp

Users with the correct privilege can change the configuration assigned to the
Ethernet ports, PRP, Bond, HSR, RSTP (not available for HU280) protocols and
routers.
IP Configuration - Devices

For each ETH port, you can set IP address, Subnet Mask, and Disable/Enable this
interface.
IP address can be set as Fixed or Automatic (using DHCP):

Redundant devices (PRP, HSR, BOND or RSTP for HU280, HUe and SM_
CPU866e) can only be configured when both of their single devices are not
configured.

54

BQT7944802-01

Working with webApp

webApp - Maintenance and Monitoring Tool

For instance, if LAN1 or LAN2 are configured with an IP address in HU280, then
PRP1, HSR1 and BOND1 are disabled:

NOTE: Multiple IPs can be configured for each interface, but these IPs must
not be on the same subnet. IPs within the same subnet cannot be configured
for different ports.
The router devices are used to define connection rules for accessing the RTU
remotely by other IP networks. It allows devices, such as tablets or PCs that are
connected to different auxiliary LANs than the RTU, to access the RTU via a WAN
within defined connection rules and limits.
IP Configuration - Routers

Refer to SE-S856-MSS - Easergy Builder User Manual for more information about
routers and ethernet ports configuration.
Routers can be added, edited or deleted depending on user’s role and rights.
Adding or editing a router

Where:

BQT7944802-01

•

Subnet IP: IP address of the auxiliary network needs access the RTU.

•

Subnet Mask: Used to define the usable IP address range on the auxiliary
network and limit the possible number of hosts.

•

Router IP: Address of the IP network gateway to which the RTU is connected.

55

webApp - Maintenance and Monitoring Tool

Working with webApp

Use 0.0.0.0 to define a default route through which communication is
automatically routed by the router when a connection is established. To do this,
simply configure the router parameters as follows:
•

Subnet IP: 0.0.0.0

•

Subnet Mask: 0.0.0.0

•

Router IP: IP address of the default gateway through which traffic is directed.

When all changes have been done, press button Save to store all modifications in
the RTU.
Depending on the configured device, the tab SNMP can be available for
configuring RTU as SNMP agent.
IP configuration - SNMP

A view is a user-defined label (collection of) subset of the MIB (Management
Information Base) tree. Each subset ID is defined by the OID (Object Identifier) of
the root of the relevant subtrees.
For each selected item in the Views list, the RTU creates a view with the selected
items. Each item in the list represents an OID (Object Identifier).
So with this section user can select what information (OID) the RTU will make
available for the SNMP manager connected to the RTU.

Click Edit SNMP user to change username, encryption algorithm or password.

Firmware and Configuration Management
In the case the system performing in an invalid state, a software watchdog resets
the device to return it to a known state. The device reset is recorded in both the
Syslog and Cyber Security log.
The watchdog can reset the device up to 5 times, then the reset is disabled.
In the case the reset is disabled, do one of the following actions:
•

If there is access to webApp: search for the debug info through webApp to
report the issue and to apply another configuration.

•

If there is no access to webApp: perform a factory reset. Once set to factory
default mode, access to webApp and follow instructions just above.

The PowerLogic HU280 does not allow invalid configurations. PowerLogic HU280
manages configurations in the following way: PowerLogic HU280 always have a
backup of the last firmware image that was loaded successfully. When the
firmware is updated, the boot loader tries to launch the new firmware.
•

If the firmware load is successful: the firmware new version overwrites the
stored backup firmware for later use.

•

If the firmware load is not successful: the backed-up firmware version is
restored.

This protects the booting process in case of the installation of an improper
firmware.

Configuration Management
The initial configuration of the RTU should be completed in Easergy Builder to
carry out the following operations:
•

Configure protocols and devices

•

Configure device synchronization

•

Configure the SOE, etc.

Refer to SE-S856-MSS - Easergy Builder User Manual for more information about
configuration of the RTU.

BQT7944802-01

•

Copy a configuration stored in a device (slot) to the PC.

•

Load other configuration (the active configuration changes).

•

Copy a configuration in the PC to a device (slot) in the CPU.

or drag and drop the file onto the Drag the configuration file here area of the
screen. The compressed file with a .tar.gz extension must be available on
the PC.
•

Slot #1, #2 or #3: Uploads the configuration directly from slot 1, 2 or 3.

4. Click Apply configuration to start uploading the configuration. A progress bar
indicates the upload status.

5. After the upload is completed, the RTU is automatically rebooted. Re-enter the
username and password to access webApp. The configuration upload is
complete.

Uploading a Configuration into a Slot
Proceed as follows to upload a previously saved configuration from the PC into
one of the slots.
1. Click Upload configuration to open the Upload configuration files window.
2. Click Select file and select the corresponding configuration file from the PC or
drag and drop the file into the Drag the configuration file here area of the
screen. The compressed file with a .tar.gz extension must be available on
the PC.

SCADA and Client Protocols
The SCADA protocols are protocols that can be used for remote communication
between the RTU and the SCADA system using any available communication
channels. These protocols are server type since the SCADA system is the client
for communication management and the RTU is the server.
Current protocols supported in webApp are: DNP3 server, IEC101 server, and
IEC104 server.
Client protocols are those protocols allowing the RTU to communicate as the
client with auxiliary equipment or an external IED installed in substations (server).
Current protocol supported in webApp is Modbus client.
Parameters displayed in webApp correspond to the application parameters of the
protocol installed in the RTU. These parameters can be customized according to
the use and the protocol parameter setting at the SCADA system end or IED.

Two synchronization sources are defined: the primary device and secondary

Glossary
A
AX160: PowerLogic T500 analog input/output module.

B
BDEW: German Association of Energy and Water Industries.

C
CAE: Cybersecurity Administrator Expert. The CAE is a tool for organizing the
T500 security policy and defining system access restrictions and user rights.
CoreDB: CoreDB is a real-time RTU database that helps ensure the RTU signals
are managed in real-time.
CPU: Central Processing Unit.
CS Phase I: Cybersecurity Phase I.

D
DHCP: Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol. A network protocol for ensuring that
station IP parameters are automatically configured via automatic IP address
allocation.

E
E3: Electrical Energy Efficiency.
Easergy Builder: Easergy Builder is the official configuration tool for T500
equipment. This tool can be used to configure all the advanced RTU functions (for
example, database, protocol addressing, events) and to carry out maintenance
tasks on the equipment.

G
GPS: Global Positioning System.

H
HSR: High-availability Seamless Redundancy.
HTTP: Hyper Text Transfer Protocol. Client-server communication protocol
developed for the World Wide Web. HTTPS (where S = Secure) is the secure
variant of HTTP using SSL or TLS protocols.
HU280: PowerLogic T500 CPU module.

I
IEC: International Electrotechnical Commission. The international standards
organization for the fields of electricity, electronics, electromagnetic compatibility,
nanotechnology, and related technologies. It complements the International
Organization for Standardization (ISO), which is responsible for other fields.
IED: Intelligent Electronic Device.
IEEE: Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers. The IEEE is a professional
association comprising members from the fields of electrical engineering,
information technology, telecommunications, etc. The organization's mission is to
advance knowledge in the field of electrical engineering and publish associated
standards and other texts written by its members.
BQT7944802-01

75

webApp - Maintenance and Monitoring Tool

IP: Internet Protocol.
IRIG-B: mode B of the standard IRIG.

L
LAN: Local Area Network.
Linux: Operating system running in realtime on the software platform. This is the
element in charge of extracting the various software components from the
hardware.

N
NERC CIP: North American Electric Reliability Corporation Critical Infrastructure
Protection plan.

O
OS: Operating System.

P
PC: Personal Computer.
PLC: Programmable Logic Controller.
PRP: Parallel Redundancy Protocol.
PTP: Precision Time Protocol.

R
RSTP: Rapid Spanning Tree Protocol.
RTDB: Real-Time DataBase.
RTOS: Real-Time Operating System.
RTU: Remote Terminal Unit.

S
SCADA: Supervisory Control And Data Acquisition.
SNMP: Simple Network Management Protocol.
SNTP: Simple Network Time Protocol.
SOE: Sequence Of Events. This relates to saving and storing events and signal
changes in the RTU that manages the data in real-time.
SSH: Secure SHell. SSH is both a program and a secure communication protocol.
It is the equivalent of the Telnet program and is used in the same way to run
certain operations remotely (mainly server administration or file transfer
operations). SSH is more secure than Telnet protocol.

T
TCP or TCP/IP: Transmission Control Protocol/Internet Protocol. Set of protocols
used to transfer data on the Internet.
TLS: Transport Security Layer.

76

BQT7944802-01

webApp - Maintenance and Monitoring Tool

W
WAN: Wide Area Network.
webUI: Advanced tool for the design and operation of a local web-based
substation user interface.

X
XS280: PowerLogic T500 serial communication module.

Safety Instructions
DANGER

HAZARD OF ELECTRIC SHOCK, EXPLOSION, OR ARC FLASH
Apply appropriate personal protective equipment (PPE) and follow safe
electrical work practices. See NFPA 70E, NOM-029-STPS-2011, CSA Z462,
NFC 18–510 and UTE C18–510–1.
This unit must be installed and serviced only by qualified electrical
personnel.
Turn off all power supplies of this unit before working on or inside the unit.
Always use a properly rated voltage sensing device to confirm that power is
off.
To open a live current transformer secondary circuit, turn off the primary side
of the transformer and short-circuit the transformer secondary circuit.
Set all devices, doors, and covers before turning on power to this unit.
Failure to follow these instructions will result in death or serious injury.

webUI – Add-on & Runtime

webUI Runtime

webUI Runtime
webApp & webUI
Saitel DP, DR and PowerLogic T500 RTUs support two web-based tools for
maintenance and monitoring:

• webApp: Embedded webserver interface for monitoring, maintenance &

diagnostics of the RTU. Using the configuration defined in Easergy Builder and
loaded on the CPU, the user can consult and / or change some parameters
through webApp. Unlike Easergy Builder, webApp does NOT allow to add new
features (and / or screens). It can only change the information previously
included through Easergy Builder using the screens already defined in the tool.

• webUI: Web-based graphical substation user interface. This tool is composed
by two different environments, one for design-time and another for run-time:

o webUI (Runtime): Web tool running in the RTU allowing to monitor the
information using screens which were designed by the user with Easergy
Builder (webUI Add- On).
o webUI (Add-On): Additional tool included in Easergy Builder for creation
and addition of customized webUI screens. It allows to design new screens
for the configuration loaded into the RTU or to modify the information in
those screens already loaded into the RTU.

Accessing webUI
webUI is accessible through a compatible web browser running in an OS Windows 7®
or higher.
The most common browsers (Firefox and Chrome) support this tool, although only
versions supporting HTML5.
Web browser

Minimal Version

Chrome

Using webApp & webUI
There are two web-based tools available: webApp and webUI.
By default, webApp is used as main web tool, that is, when the user writes
https://<CPU IP address> in the address bar of the web browser, by default, the main
page of webApp is shown.

dismissed to load the website. For example, in Microsoft Edge select 'Go on to the
webpage'.

Graphic Representation Zone (Zone 2)
The information displayed in the graphic representation area depends on the option
selected in the main menu.
Graphic representation zone

The first screen in the main menu is shown by default. The order of the available
screens can be changed using Easergy Builder.
In this zone it is possible to zoom and pan. Zooming is done with the mouse wheel
and panning can be done with the left-click, right-click or also with the mouse wheel.
When the window is in its original size, no panning is allowed.
Finally, to reset the view it would only be necessary to double left-click to do it.

Latest Alarms Zone (Zone 3)
This zone shows the latest three alarms. The visual appearance of each alarm line
will depend on its status and on the user acknowledge.
• Blinking: Unacknowledged alarm
• Colored according to the user configuration: Active alarm and Inactive alarm
colors are configured by the user in the Easergy Builder Add-On. More
information in section Alarm Levels.

Example of acquisition screen

Alarms

More information in chapter webUI Editor.

Selecting button

> Alarms, the alarm page is shown. In this list are included:

• Acknowledged active alarms.
• Unacknowledged active alarms.
• Unacknowledged inactive alarms
Acknowledging an alarm will make it stop blinking. To acknowledge a specific
alarm, it is necessary to use the button “Acknowledge” in that row. There are two
more buttons: “Acknowledge all” and “Acknowledge page”. The first is used to
knowledge all activated alarms, while the second is used to acknowledge only the
page where the user is at that moment.
However, there is a particular case where it is necessary to use the “Acknowledge
page” or the specific “Acknowledge” and that is when the alarm corresponds to a
supervision point. “Acknowledge all” will not acknowledge alarms which correspond
to supervision points.
Alarms page

The color of the alarm is configurable in Easergy Builder. More information in
paragraph Alarm Levels.
Alarms are, by default, ordered by the column 'Timestamp'. The arrow next to it can
be used to show most recent or oldest first.
For each signal, the displayed information is platform dependent:

Public

BQT7944802-00

webUI – Add-on & Runtime

webUI Runtime

Alarms page (PowerLogic T500 engineering view)

• Integrated view + Engineering: Available columns are TIMESTAMP, VALUE,
QUALITY, B1, B2, B3, ELEMENT and INFO
Alarms page (PowerLogic T500 integrated + engineering view)

The meanings of these fields are:
• ALARM: Defines if the signal es in alarm status with a blinking red “A”. This
column name is not visible.
• TIMESTAMP: Date and time associated to the alarm.
• VALUE: Value of the signal. For digital signals, the value is shown in text
format, and for analog signals the numerical value is used.
• QUALITY: Signal quality.
• B1: The text indicated in this column will be applied to the engineering field B1
assigned to the point in the webUI configuration.
• B2: The text indicated in this column will be applied to the engineering field B2
assigned to the point in the webUI configuration.
• B3: The text indicated in this column will be applied to the engineering field B3
assigned to the point in the webUI configuration.
• ELEMENT: The text indicated in this column will be applied to the Engineering
Element field assigned to the point in the webUI configuration.
• POINT NAME: Signal name in coreDb.
• POSITION: Source device of the information associated with the signal (field
Source Device).
• SOURCE: Coordinates of the signal in coreDb (field Source Coordinates).
• DESCRIPTION: Brief description of the signal (field Description in coreDb).
• ALARM TYPE: Indicates the “Alarm Mode” defined in Easergy Builders real
time table.
The information shown in the previous fields is configured for each signal in the
page 'Realtime configuration' of Easergy Builder webUI Add-Ons as follow:
• VALUE: Text included in field A0 label, A1 label, A2 label or A3 label
according to the signal value (0, 1, 2 or 3).
• B1, B2 and B3: Texts include in columns B1, B2 and B3 respectively.
• ELEMENT: Text included in the column Element.
• INFO: Text included in the column Info.
Clicking on any of these elements allows the user to order the alarms depending on
the value of that element.

List of signals in database

For each signal the following information is displayed:
• TIMESTAMP: Date and time of the last change of value or quality.
• VALUE: For status and command points, label assigned in Easergy Builder to
the current value of the signal. This label is set in the Realtime Configuration
window in Easergy Builder. If no label has been assigned, the test NA (not
apply) is shown. For analog and setpoint, this field shows the current value of
the signal. More information in section Realtime Configuration.
• QUALITY: Quality information.
• POINT NAME: Signal name in coreDb.
• POSITION: Source device of the information associated with the signal (field
Source Device).
• SOURCE: Coordinates of the signal in coreDb (field Source Coordinates).
• DESCRIPTION: Brief description of the signal (field Description in coreDb).

Chronological events

The Chronological window shows all events that occur in the system, ordered by
the timestamp, being the first record in the list the most recent.
The number of events in the list will depend on the depth marked in the SOE
configuration in Easergy Builder. More information in the SOE Device user manual.
For each signal the following information is displayed:
• TIMESTAMP: Date and time of last value or quality change.

Dynamic Elements
Any screen can include two different types of symbols associated to field devices:
• Informative. This type of symbol is oriented to show signal values, status
information or any other data available in database.
• Controllable Elements. The associated device in field allows to be operated.
When a symbol on the screen is selected (left clicking with the mouse), a pop-up
window appears including information about the associated signals and operation
buttons if the device allows to be operated.

Informative Symbols
If an element does not allow operation, when right-clicking on it, a window similar to
the following one is shown:
Window of informative symbols

Where:
• Position: name of the equipment where the signal comes from.
• Name: name of the point.
• Description: descriptive text of the signal.
• Value: numerical value of the signal.
• Quality: quality information based on icons. More information below.

webUI – Add-on & Runtime

webUI Runtime

• Hour: timestamp of last value change.
• Status: state of the signal.
Click button EXIT to close the window.

Controllable Symbols
To understand how to use controllable symbols it is necessary to know first how
Local and Remote modes work.
First, the system mode can be modified as explained in section Settings Tool.
The difference between Local and Remote modes is the execution of commands.
For Local it is possible to execute them while in Remote mode it is not.
More information about activating commands and controllable symbols can be
found below.
Controllable Symbols can only be operated while webUI is in Local mode and the
current user has the suitable rights to execute the action (for instance, Viewer role
do not have permission to execute controllable symbols).
All commands are SBO (Select Before Operate), that is, commands are executed in
two phases, selection and execution.
When the user right clicks on a controllable element, a window will be shown
including operation buttons (according to the active configuration) and real-time
information in coreDb.
Window of controllable symbols

The operation button will be shown when CONTROL button is pressed. While the
command is not selected, the text 'Not selected' is shown in red.

Executing a command

To send the command to field, button EXECUTE must be pressed.
When in Remote mode, trying to execute a command will make a message appear,
saying “REMOTE commands not allowed”, as it can be seen in the following figure.
Executing a command in Remote mode

The Execute command is not allowed until the command is selected. To execute a
command user must press buttons in the following order: CONTROL, SELECT and
EXECUTE.
Finally, using 'Command lock' or 'Interlock' function, a command can be blocked
depending on the value of other elements in coreDb. More information in section
Command Locks.

Quality Information
The icon displayed next to each value, provides information about the quality of the
status or value shown. This information is shown too in the Signal list for each
signal.
The quality icon information is associated to a hexadecimal value, and it is
calculated based on a combination of each quality bit. Other data to be considered
is the status Local or Remote.

Measures
Several types of predefined measurements are available to be included in the
webUI screens. Some properties of these values, such as font, size or associated
text, can be changed using Easergy Builder as it is explained in the following
chapter of this manual.
The color associated to the value can be configured by the user.
Each measurement needs to be linked to a coreDb signal and its value will be
shown in real-time in webUI. Parameters like color, letter font, size, etc. will be
configurable. The “Units” parameter, which is used to describe the unit of
measurement, will be only available for “Measures” and not for “Analog value”.

Settings Tool
Using the setting tool

, it is possible to:

• Restart the CPU or change the status between local and remote.
• Go to webApp.
• Manage interlocks.
• Activate / Deactivate sound for alarms.
• Activate / Deactivate pop-up windows of the dynamic elements on the
screens.
• Change the default language of webUI.
• Have information about the current webUI.

BQT7944803-EN-00

Public

29

webUI – Add-on & Runtime

webUI Runtime

Settings tool

Using System option, the following window is shown:
System operations

Press RESET to reboot the CPU or CHANGE L/R STATE to change between local
and remote control of the RTU.
After the button is pressed, the text Correct (green) or Error (red) is shown
depending on the operation was successfully executed or not.
To be able to use these buttons, the following signals must be defined in coreDb:
• For Local/Remote button: Table: Status, Source: supervision device,
Coordinate: LOCAL:W.
• However, there is something specific about this signal. If it is also mapped
with Destination: supervision device and Coordinate: LOCAL, if the signal
value is valid, then webUI does not allow to use the button to alternate
between Local and Remote modes. If it has an invalid value, it will appear as
“Unknown” (
) and webUI does not allow either to use the button.
• For Reset button: Table: Command, Coordinate: RESET_RTU.
Both signals must be configured as Enable in Realtime Configuration window in
Easergy Builder. More information in following chapter.
NOTICE
HAZARD OF INAPROPRIATE OPERATION
Before pressing RESET button, check that there is not a valid operation on
course: There is no confirmation required and the RTU will be rebooted
immediately.
Failure to follow these instructions can result in an improper operation.

Interlocks
To access the list of interlocks defined in webUI, select button

> Interlocks.

Interlocks in webUI
More information about how interlocks can be modified or created can be found in
Command Locks section.

webUI – Add-on & Runtime

webUI Editor

webUI Editor
webUI Description
The webUI Editor is designed as an Add-On included in the Easergy Builder
configuration tool.
In the configuration environment of Easergy Builder, on the main menu, select AddOns > webUI Configuration. If this option is not available, install the plugin
'webUI_SPlugin.msi' supplied in the Easergy Builder installation package.
webUI configuration tool completes the functionality of Easergy Builder with the
necessary functions to perform the configuration of the embedded webUI system.
This tool offers a series of windows to allow the monitoring and control of the
system.
With these considerations, webUI Configuration for Easergy Builder allows to
configure the screens included in the system, as well as the graphical objects that
will be represented in each of them.
webUI Editor

The webUI Editor is shown as one more tab in Easergy Builder (marked in blue in
the figure above).
This window has five different areas:
• Zone 1: a toolbar that includes a series of buttons with the following features:
•

Show or hide the different areas of the editor.

•

Show and hide the design grid.

•

Manage and use the graphical display repository.

•

Access to the editing help tools (object alignment).

•

Preview the selected screen.

• Zone 2: name and description of the screens created in the system, presented
in a hierarchical way.
• Zone 3: tree of graphic objects available to be used on the screens.
• Zone 4: editor area, where the user can design the aspect that will show in
real-time the screen selected in zone 2.
• Zone 5: configuration area, where screens, database and settings can be
configured.

Hiding a Screen
To hide a screen from the runtime, select it, right click, and choose “Hide screen”. In
this case, the symbol
which appears on the left will turn its color to red
.
This means when the configuration is uploaded to the RTU, this screen will not
appear as an option.
If a screen is hidden, to make it visible again it would only be necessary to select it,
right click and choose “Make screen visible”. Then the symbol will turn back from
red to green.

Graphic Objects (Zone 3)
The main webUI configuration zone contains a tree of graphic objects where the
objects included in the loaded library are presented. Using these objects, new
graphic elements can be added to the active screen.
To do this, select an object type on the tree (it will be highlighted in blue), drag and
drop on the screen. When the object is located on the screen, clicking right-button,
its properties can be changed according to the requirements of the project.
Following sections show the available properties for dynamic and static objects. The
most of them are common for all object types and only some object types could
have properties which are explained below too.

webUI Editor

This window shows the set of points registered in the database, according to the
type of point selected in the upper selection box. Select a point type and click on the
apply filter button to display the points.

Realtime Configuration
This tab allows to configure the coreDb points that will be managed by the webUI,
indicating for each of them the specific parameters to be applied.
The presentation is divided in four tabs, Status, Analog, Command and Setpoint.
Each tab presents the list of points of the indicated type registered in the coreDb.
For each coreDb signal to be managed by webUI the field Enabled must be
enabled.
Following pictures show how signals between WARN_PS1 and FAIL_PS1 are not
shown in the Signal page of webUI.
Configuration of signals in webUI

Signals in webUI

Status Point
For each enabled point, the following parameters can be configured:
• Name: Signal name.
• Description: Signal description.
• Alarm mode: Indicates if the point generates alarms or not. It is possible to
select the alarm level that applies to it. See section Alarm Levels for more
details.

BQT7944803-EN-00

Public

51

webUI – Add-on & Runtime

webUI Editor

• Point type: There are two types of points:
•

SP: Single point. The value of the associated signal can be 0 or 1.

•

DP: Double point. The value of the associated signal can be 0, 1, 2 or 3.

• B1, B2, B3, Element e Info: texts associated to the engineering information of
the points.
• A0 label: Text to be shown when the value of the signal is 0.
• A1 label: Text to be shown when the value of the signal is 1.
• A2 label: Text to be shown when the value of the signal is 2 (double status
signals).
• A3 label: Text to be shown when the value of the signal is 3 (double status
signals).

Alarm Configuration
Each status signal configured in the webUI can be configurated to generate alarms
for a specific value or when the value changes.
When a status signal is marked as Enabled, by default, Alarm mode field is None,
that is, no alarm will be generated for this point.
To configure a status point to generate alarms, press on the field Alarm mode.
Selection of status point for alarm configuration

The following window is shown.
Alarm configuration window

In field Alarm mode, select the signal value for which the alarm will be activated.
• None: No signal value will generate alarm.
• On: An alarm will be activated when the signal is ON. Depending on the Point
type, single (SP) or double (DP), the alarm will be activated when the signal
value is 1 (SP and DP).
• Off: An alarm will be activated when the signal is OFF. Depending on the
Point type, single (SP) or double (DP), the alarm will be activated when the
signal value is 0 (SP and DP).
• Both: Any value of the point will activate an alarm.

Command Points
For each enabled command point, the following parameters can be configured:
• Point type: Point type indicator. There are two types of points:
•

SC: Single command. When this type of point is used, the element can be
changed between 0 and 1.

•

DC: Double command. When this type of point is used, the element can be
changed between 0, 1, 2 and 3.

• B1, B2, B3, Element e Info: Text fields for engineering information.
• A0 label: Text to be shown when the value of the signal is 0.
• A1 label: Text to be shown when the value of the signal is 1.
• A2 label: Text to be shown when the value of the signal is 2 (double status
signals).
• A3 label: Text to be shown when the value of the signal is 3 (double status
signals).
• Locks: This column gives access to the configuration of the locks applied to
the execution of the command.

Command Locks Configuration
For each command configured in the webUI system locks can be associated, so
that the execution of the command is only possible if all locks are deactivated.
This configuration can be accessed from the command view of the webUI Realtime
Configuration section, by pressing the button in the column Locks of the command
point.
Selection of command point for lock configuration

Alarm Levels
This webUI Configuration option allows to configure the alarm levels that will be
managed by the webUI and that will determine how the alarms will be presented to
the user.
Each alarm level has a customizable set of colors to be presented as active or nonactive alarms. It is possible to identify the signals that will be treated as alarms and
assign them alarm levels. webUI will present each alarm using the set of colors
associated for each level.

with the right or left mouse click on the element.
Access to the command window with right click setting

• Local lock enabled: When False, it is not possible to change the Local status
in the webUI/System section.

Glossary
A
AC: Alternate Current.
ACK: Acknowledgement.

B
Bps: Bits per second.
BL: Locked

C

CA: Reset.

COT: Cause of Transmission.
CPU: Central Processing Unit.
CY: Carry.

D
DC: Direct Current.
DI: Digital Input.
DIN: Deutsches Institut für Normung.
DO: Digital Output.

E
Easergy Builder: Configuration tool for Saitel and PowerLogic T500.

G
GMT: Greenwich Mean Time. Mean solar time at the Royal Observatory in Greenwich,
London, England, used as the universal time standard.

H
HMI: Human Machine Interface.
HTTP: Hyper Text Transfer Protocol. Client-server communication protocol developed for
the World Wide Web. HTTPS (where S=Secure) is the secure variant of HTTP using SSL
or TLS protocols.
